Or allocate in C++. Let's have the C++ wrappers allocate output tensors and launch kernels. Example: ```cpp torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu_cuda( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups) { int B = input.size(0); int in_c = input.size(1); int H = input.size(2); int W = input.size(3); auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, input.options()); const int threads = 256; const int blocks = (B*H*W + threads - 1) / threads; shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, in_c, out_c, groups); return output; } ``` Similarly for the others. **Optimization for small sizes:** Our block size is 256. For small tensors, this is fine. **Handling boundaries in depthwise:** We have `h2 = h + kh`. If out of bounds, skip (or effectively multiply by 0, since padding=1 in the reference). Wait: The reference uses `padding=1` for depthwise 3x3. So boundaries are handled by padding with zeros. In our kernel, if `h2` or `w2` is out of bounds, we just don't add anything (equivalent to zero padding). Good. **Potential issue: `groups` is not divisible or odd?** Reference groups=3. mid_c = out_c // 4. `out_c % 4 == 0`. And `groups` divides `out_c`? Not necessarily. But for ShuffleNet, `mid_c` is usually chosen to be divisible by `groups`. In the reference, `conv1` is `nn.Conv2d(in_channels, mid_channels, groups=groups)`. This requires `in_channels % groups == 0` and `mid_channels % groups == 0`. The code doesn't assert this, but standard ShuffleNet architectures ensure it. For the given config: stages_out_channels = [24, 240, 480, 960]. out_c % 4 = 0. mid_c = out_c//4. in_c for first unit of stage2 is 24. Does 24 % 3 == 0? Yes. mid_c = 240//4 = 60. 60 % 3 == 0. Good. For stage3: in_c=240, 240%3=0. mid_c=480//4=120, 120%3=0. For stage4: in_c=480, 480%3=0. mid_c=960//4=240, 240%3=0. So everything works. **First and last layer fusion:** `conv1` in Model is `nn.Conv2d(3, 24, k=3, s=2, p=1)`. We can fuse BN1. `conv5` is `nn.Conv2d(960, 1024, k=1)`. We can fuse BN5. In `forward`: ```python x = F.relu(F.conv2d(x, fused_w1, fused_b1, stride=2, padding=1)) x = F.max_pool2d(x, kernel_size=3, stride=2, padding=1) ``` For `conv5`: ```python x = F.relu(F.conv2d(x, fused_w5, fused_b5)) ``` We could also write custom kernels for these, but they are not the main bottleneck. However, `F.conv2d` + `F.relu_` is 2 ops. If we use `F.relu(F.conv2d(...))`, the relu is fused into conv by PyTorch's cuDNN backend if possible? In eager mode, PyTorch's `conv2d` calls cuDNN and writes output. Then `relu` is a separate kernel. But for `stride=2, 3->24`, it's tiny. For `conv5`: `960->1024`, spatial 56x56. 1x1 conv. This is a dense conv, equivalent to a GEMM. PyTorch will call cuDNN/cuBLAS. It's likely well optimized. But it's 960*1024*56*56 = 3B FLOPs. We might want to keep it. **Adaptive average pool:** `x = F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1,1))` is equivalent to `x.mean(dim=(2,3))` or `x.mean((2,3), keepdim=True)`. The latter is a reduce mean, which is efficient. Then view. We can do: `x = x.mean(dim=(2,3))` # shape [B, 1024] Then `x = F.linear(x, self.fc.weight, self.fc.bias)`. **Implementation plan:** 1. Define `ModelNew`. 2. In `__init__`, construct the same architecture to get weights? Or we can accept a `Model` instance and copy weights? The specification says `ModelNew` must accept the same constructor arguments as `Model`. So we need to instantiate layers or at least generate weights. But we can instantiate `nn.Conv2d`, etc., and then fuse weights into our custom parameters. Or we can just create the modules and in `forward` use fused weights. Actually, we need the weights for the custom kernels. We can create the reference `Model` inside `ModelNew.__init__` to get all the weights, then fuse them. But `Model` is not defined in our module unless we import it. The evaluation environment has `Model` defined. But to be safe, we can re-implement the layer creation logic in `ModelNew.__init__` using `nn.Conv2d`, `nn.BatchNorm2d`, etc., and then process them to fused weights. The problem says `ModelNew` class must accept same constructor args. It doesn't say we can't instantiate submodules. So in `ModelNew.__init__`: ```python super().__init__() self.groups = groups # ... create layers same as Model ... # Then fuse weights and move to CUDA ``` But if we keep them as `nn.Conv2d`, `forward` might accidentally use them. We can store the fused tensors as `self.w1_stage2_unit0` etc. That would be a lot of manual bookkeeping. Alternatively, we can build a list of stages as Python lists of dicts containing fused tensors. For example: ```python self.stages = [] for stage_idx, repeats in enumerate(stages_repeats): stage_units = [] in_c = stages_out_channels[stage_idx] out_c = stages_out_channels[stage_idx+1] for i in range(repeats): unit_in_c = in_c if i == 0 else out_c # create unit, fuse weights, store in dict stage_units.append({ 'w1': fused_w1, 'b1': fused_b1, 'w2': fused_w2, 'b2': fused_b2, 'w3': fused_w3, 'b3': fused_b3, 'ws': fused_ws, 'bs': fused_bs, # if has_shortcut 'in_c': unit_in_c, 'mid_c': out_c//4, 'out_c': out_c, }) self.stages.append(stage_units) ``` This is manageable. 3. `forward(self, x)`: - x = conv1_kernel or `F.conv2d(x, self.conv1_w, self.conv1_b, stride=2, padding=1); x = F.relu_(x)` - x = F.max_pool2d(x, ...) - for each stage in self.stages: for unit in stage: mid = custom_conv1(x, unit['w1'], unit['b1'], unit['in_c'], unit['mid_c'], self.groups) mid_s = custom_depthwise(mid, unit['w2'], unit['b2'], unit['mid_c'], self.groups) x = custom_conv3_add(mid_s, x, unit['w3'], unit['b3'], unit.get('ws'), unit.get('bs'), unit['mid_c'], unit['out_c'], self.groups, unit['in_c'], has_shortcut) - x = F.conv2d(x, self.conv5_w, self.conv5_b); x = F.relu_(x) - x = x.mean(dim=(2,3)) - x = F.linear(x, self.fc.weight, self.fc.bias) - return x Wait: For `custom_conv3_add`, the `x_orig` passed is the *input to the unit*. For identity shortcut, we need `x_orig` to have `in_c` channels, and we add `x_orig[:, o, h, w]`. But note: the units are in a Sequential stage. The output of unit i is the input to unit i+1. So for unit i+1, `x_orig` is the output from previous unit. In the first unit of a stage, `x_orig` is the input to that unit. For subsequent units, `x_orig` has `out_c` channels. In our loop, we can keep `prev_x = x`, compute `mid`, `mid_s`, then compute `x = custom_conv3_add(mid_s, prev_x, ...)`. Yes. **Writing the C++ and CUDA code:** Let's draft the code more carefully. ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> __global__ void shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int in_c, int out_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int in_cpg = in_c / groups; int out_cpg = out_c / groups; int base_in = ((b * in_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_out = ((b * out_c) * H + h) * W + w; for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { int g = o / out_cpg; float sum = bias[o]; int w_base = o * in_cpg; int in_off = base_in + g * in_cpg * H * W; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < in_cpg; ++i) { sum += input[in_off + i * H * W] * weight[w_base + i]; } output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } // Depthwise + shuffle write __global__ void shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups; // Iterate over original channels for (int c = 0; c < mid_c; ++c) { float sum = bias[c]; int w_base = c * 9; #pragma unroll for (int kh = -1; kh <= 1; ++kh) { int h2 = h + kh; if (h2 < 0 || h2 >= H) continue; int in_row_off = ((b * mid_c + c) * H + h2) * W; int w_row_off = w_base + (kh + 1) * 3; #pragma unroll for (int kw = -1; kw <= 1; ++kw) { int w2 = w + kw; if (w2 < 0 || w2 >= W) continue; sum += input[in_row_off + w2] * weight[w_row_off + (kw + 1)]; } } // Compute logical channel after shuffle int logical_c = (c % mid_cpg) * groups + (c / mid_cpg); output[((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w + logical_c * H * W] = sum; } } // Conv3 + add + relu __global__ void shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel( const float* __restrict__ mid, const float* __restrict__ x_orig, const float* __restrict__ w3, const float* __restrict__ b3, const float* __restrict__ ws, const float* __restrict__ bs, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int out_c, int groups, int in_c, int has_shortcut) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups; int out_cpg = out_c / groups; int base_mid = ((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_out = ((b * out_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_x = ((b * in_c) * H + h) * W + w; for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { int g = o / out_cpg; float sum = b3[o]; int w_base = o * mid_cpg; int mid_off = base_mid + g * mid_cpg * H * W; // Unrolling may help for small mid_cpg (20, 40, 80) for (int i = 0; i < mid_cpg; ++i) { sum += mid[mid_off + i * H * W] * w3[w_base + i]; } if (has_shortcut) { float s = bs ? bs[o] : 0.0f; // actually bs is always provided with ws int ws_base = o * in_c; for (int i = 0; i < in_c; ++i) { s += x_orig[base_x + i * H * W] * ws[ws_base + i]; } sum += s; } else { // identity shortcut sum += x_orig[base_out + o * H * W]; } output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } ``` And wrapper functions: ```cpp torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups) { int B = input.size(0); int in_c = input.size(1); int H = input.size(2); int W = input.size(3); auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, input.options()); const int threads = 256; const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads; shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, in_c, out_c, groups); return output; } torch::Tensor shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle( torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int groups) { int B = input.size(0); int mid_c = input.size(1); int H = input.size(2); int W = input.size(3); auto output = torch::empty_like(input); const int threads = 256; const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads; shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>( input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, mid_c, groups); return output; } torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv3_add( torch::Tensor mid, torch::Tensor x_orig, torch::Tensor w3, torch::Tensor b3, c10::optional<torch::Tensor> ws, c10::optional<torch::Tensor> bs, int out_c, int groups) { int B = mid.size(0); int mid_c = mid.size(1); int H = mid.size(2); int W = mid.size(3); int in_c = x_orig.size(1); auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, mid.options()); const int threads = 256; const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads; int has_shortcut = ws.has_value() ? 1 : 0; shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>( mid.data_ptr<float>(), x_orig.data_ptr<float>(), w3.data_ptr<float>(), b3.data_ptr<float>(), has_shortcut ? ws.value().data_ptr<float>() : nullptr, has_shortcut ? bs.value().data_ptr<float>() : nullptr, output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, mid_c, out_c, groups, in_c, has_shortcut); return output; } ``` Wait, identity shortcut: `x_orig` has shape `[B, in_c, H, W]`. If `in_c == out_c`, we add `x_orig[:, o, h, w]`. But if `in_c != out_c`, we have a 1x1 conv shortcut. In that case, `x_orig` is the input with `in_c` channels. The output is `out_c`. In the kernel, for `has_shortcut==0` (identity), we do `sum += x_orig[base_x + o * H * W]`. This assumes `in_c == out_c`. For `has_shortcut==1`, we compute the dense conv. Now, for the first unit of a stage, `in_c != out_c`. We pass `ws` and `bs`. For subsequent units, `in_c == out_c`. We pass `ws=None`, `bs=None`. One more thing: The `base_x` for identity shortcut is computed as `((b * in_c) * H + h) * W + w`. For `o`, the offset is `o * H * W`. Correct. **Weight flattening in Python:** The kernels expect 1D arrays. For `w1`: shape `[out_c, in_c/g, 1, 1]`. Flatten to `[out_c * in_c/g]`. The CUDA code reads `w_base + i`. For `w2`: shape `[mid_c, 1, 3, 3]`. Flatten to `[mid_c, 9]`. Or `[mid_c * 9]`. For `w3`: shape `[out_c, mid_c/g, 1, 1]`. Flatten. For `ws`: shape `[out_c, in_c, 1, 1]`. Flatten to `[out_c * in_c]`. **Fusing weights:** Helper function: ```python def fuse_conv_bn(conv, bn): w = conv.weight mean = bn.running_mean var = bn.running_var gamma = bn.weight beta = bn.bias eps = bn.eps std = torch.sqrt(var + eps) w_fused = w * (gamma / std).view(-1, 1, 1, 1) b_fused = beta - gamma * mean / std return w_fused, b_fused ``` For depthwise, `conv.weight` shape `[mid_c, 1, 3, 3]`. `(gamma/std).view(-1, 1, 1, 1)` works. `b_fused` shape `[mid_c]`. **Potential numerical issue:** Our kernels use float32. The reference uses PyTorch's default float32. We need to match within `1e-4`. Rounding error from manual loops vs cuDNN might differ slightly, but should be within tolerance. The depthwise conv uses the same arithmetic order (9 terms) as cuDNN? cuDNN might use different reduction order, causing small differences. Since tolerance is `1e-4`, it should be okay. But to be safe, we could use `float` accumulation. We are using `float` (32-bit). That's fine. **Compile and test:** We will need to compile the inline CUDA code. Let's draft the full Python code. Wait, the `custom_conv1` kernel: we use it for the unit's `conv1`, but what about the first `conv1` of the network? It's a 3x3 stride 2. We can just use `F.conv2d` for that. Similarly, `conv5` is 1x1 dense conv. We can use `F.conv2d`. **Optimizing the custom kernels further:** We can use `__launch_bounds__(256)` to hint the compiler. We can try `blockDim.x = 512` to process more pixels per block and keep more warps active? Actually total work is fixed. `blockDim.x` changes parallelism within a block. With 256 threads, each block handles 256 pixels. That's 2 warps of 32? No, 8 warps. Good. If we use 128 threads, 4 warps. Still okay. But 256 is standard. In the `shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel`, the inner loop `for i < mid_cpg` is small. We can add `#pragma unroll` if we pass `mid_cpg` as a template parameter? But we pass it as a runtime variable, so the compiler cannot unroll unless it sees the constant. CUDA compiler doesn't unroll variable loops. But we can add `#pragma unroll` anyway; it might unroll if the trip count is known at compile time from a constant expression, but here it's a kernel argument (loaded from constant memory). The NVCC compiler might not unroll it. However, loop trip counts are small (20, 40, 80). We could use a `switch` or `if` template specialization by generating multiple kernels, but that's overkill. One optimization: in `conv1` and `conv3`, instead of each thread looping over all output channels, we can have the block loop over output channel tiles and use shared memory for weights. For example, load `w3` for a tile of output channels into shared memory, then all threads compute dot products for those channels. This avoids reading weights from global memory repeatedly per pixel. Since weights are small (e.g., `w3` for 960->240: 960*80=76,800 floats = 307KB). That's small enough to fit in L2 cache. And each warp reads the same weights sequentially. So weight cache hit rate should be high. Not a big bottleneck. Similarly, `mid_s` is read sequentially per group. I think the kernels are reasonable. **Let's write the full code.** One caveat: The `load_inline` will be called at module load time. We need to ensure we include `<torch/extension.h>` and use `at::Tensor` / `torch::Tensor`. The `functions` list in `load_inline` must match the C++ wrapper function names. We need to make sure the `cpp_sources` string includes the CUDA kernel declarations (or we can put everything in `cuda_sources` and just wrappers in `cpp_sources`). `load_inline` syntax: ```python import torch.utils.cpp_extension cuda_ext = torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline( name="shufflenet_cuda", cpp_sources=cpp_source, cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=['shufflenet_conv1_relu', 'shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle', 'shufflenet_conv3_add'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', '--use_fast_math'], verbose=False, ) ``` Let's draft the source strings. cpp_source: ```cpp #include <torch/extension.h> // CUDA forward declarations torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu_cuda(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups); torch::Tensor shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_cuda(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int groups); torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv3_add_cuda(torch::Tensor mid, torch::Tensor x_orig, torch::Tensor w3, torch::Tensor b3, c10::optional<torch::Tensor> ws, c10::optional<torch::Tensor> bs, int out_c, int groups); // wrappers torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups) { return shufflenet_conv1_relu_cuda(input, weight, bias, out_c, groups); } ... ``` Or define everything in the same `cuda_sources` string and have `cpp_sources` just include the declarations and wrappers. Actually, with `load_inline`, you put kernel code in `cuda_sources` and host wrappers in `cpp_sources`. The host wrappers call the kernels. Let's define everything cleanly. Full Python file structure: ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn import torch.nn.functional as F import torch.utils.cpp_extension # Load inline CUDA cuda_ext = torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline(...) class ModelNew(nn.Module): def __init__(self, num_classes=1000, groups=3, stages_repeats=[3,7,3], stages_out_channels=[24,240,480,960]): super().__init__() self.groups = groups # Helper to fuse conv+bn def fuse(conv, bn): ... # Build first conv+bn conv1 = nn.Conv2d(3, stages_out_channels[0], 3, stride=2, padding=1, bias=False) bn1 = nn.BatchNorm2d(stages_out_channels[0]) self.conv1_w, self.conv1_b = fuse(conv1, bn1) self.maxpool = nn.MaxPool2d(3, stride=2, padding=1) # Build stages self.units = nn.ModuleList() # or python list in_ch = stages_out_channels[0] for rep, out_ch in zip(stages_repeats, stages_out_channels[1:]): for i in range(rep): unit_in = in_ch if i == 0 else out_ch # create unit unit = ShuffleNetUnit(unit_in, out_ch, groups) # fuse all weights w1, b1 = fuse(unit.conv1, unit.bn1) w2, b2 = fuse(unit.conv2, unit.bn2) w3, b3 = fuse(unit.conv3, unit.bn3) if isinstance(unit.shortcut, nn.Sequential): ws, bs = fuse(unit.shortcut[0], unit.shortcut[1]) else: ws = bs = None # flatten to 1D self.units.append({ 'in_c': unit_in, 'mid_c': out_ch // 4, 'out_c': out_ch, 'w1': w1.view(-1), 'b1': b1, 'w2': w2.view(-1), 'b2': b2, 'w3': w3.view(-1), 'b3': b3, 'ws': ws.view(-1) if ws is not None else None, 'bs': bs if bs is not None else None, }) in_ch = out_ch # Build conv5+bn5 conv5 = nn.Conv2d(stages_out_channels[3], 1024, 1, bias=False) bn5 = nn.BatchNorm2d(1024) self.conv5_w, self.conv5_b = fuse(conv5, bn5) self.fc = nn.Linear(1024, num_classes) # Move to CUDA? Actually weights are on CPU until forward? We'll register as buffers/parameters. # Better: self.register_buffer('conv1_w', fused_w1) ``` Wait: `self.units` as a list of dicts with tensors. These tensors will be registered as parameters/buffers automatically if assigned as attributes. But in a list, PyTorch doesn't track them. We can use `nn.ParameterList` or `nn.ModuleList` of dummy modules. Or simply register buffer names like `unit0_w1`. That's tedious. A simpler approach: just create the `Model` reference inside `ModelNew`, copy its weights, and then in `forward` call the reference's submodules? No, the whole point is to replace forward. We can use a list of dicts and call `.to(device)` on the tensors before using them. But PyTorch won't track them for `model.cuda()`. However, the test code might call `model = ModelNew(...); model.cuda()`. Actually, looking at the prompt, the test code just does `get_inputs()` and presumably runs on CUDA if available? The prompt says "the kernel will run on a GPU". So we might need to ensure tensors are CUDA. Because the inputs are CUDA tensors, operations will fail if weights are CPU. But if we create the model and move it to CUDA (if the testing framework does), then buffers need to be registered. The safer way is: ```python self.units = [] for i, unit_params in enumerate(list_of_params): self.units.append(unit_params) ``` Then in `forward`, when we call the custom kernels, we pass the tensors from `self.units[i]`. If `self.cuda()` is called, PyTorch won't move these tensors because they are not attributes. So we should register them: ```python for stage_idx in range(...): for unit_idx in range(...): unit = {...} for key, val in unit.items(): if isinstance(val, torch.Tensor): self.register_buffer(f"s{stage_idx}_u{unit_idx}_{key}", val) elif val is None: pass # can't register None # store names or a flat list ``` But constructing the attribute names and retrieving them in forward is doable. Let's do this: ```python self.unit_keys = [] idx = 0 for stage_idx, rep in enumerate(stages_repeats): for u in range(rep): prefix = f"u{idx}_" # register buffers for k, v in unit.items(): if isinstance(v, torch.Tensor): self.register_buffer(prefix + k, v) self.unit_keys.append(prefix) idx += 1 ``` In `forward`: ```python for prefix in self.unit_keys: w1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w1') b1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b1') ... ``` This ensures `.cuda()` moves them. Similarly for `conv1_w`, `conv1_b`, `conv5_w`, `conv5_b`. `self.fc` is an `nn.Linear`. We keep it as a module. `self.maxpool` can be `nn.MaxPool2d` module. Actually we can just call `F.max_pool2d`. **Drafting the full code:** Let's write it. Note: `ModelNew` should not rely on `Model` class. We'll re-implement unit creation. ```python class ShuffleNetUnit(nn.Module): def __init__(self, in_c, out_c, groups): super().__init__() ... ``` We can just copy the `ShuffleNetUnit` and `ChannelShuffle` code for weight initialization. Now, `forward` of `ModelNew`: ```python def forward(self, x): x = F.conv2d(x, self.conv1_w, self.conv1_b, stride=2, padding=1) x = F.relu_(x) x = F.max_pool2d(x, kernel_size=3, stride=2, padding=1) for prefix in self.unit_keys: in_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'in_c') mid_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'mid_c') out_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'out_c') w1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w1') b1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b1') w2 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w2') b2 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b2') w3 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w3') b3 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b3') ws = getattr(self, prefix + 'ws', None) bs = getattr(self, prefix + 'bs', None) has_shortcut = ws is not None mid = cuda_ext.shufflenet_conv1_relu(x, w1, b1, mid_c, self.groups) mid_s = cuda_ext.shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(mid, w2, b2, self.groups) if has_shortcut: x = cuda_ext.shufflenet_conv3_add(mid_s, x, w3, b3, ws, bs, out_c, self.groups) else: x = cuda_ext.shufflenet_conv3_add(mid_s, x, w3, b3, None, None, out_c, self.groups) x = F.conv2d(x, self.conv5_w, self.conv5_b) x = F.relu_(x) x = x.mean(dim=(2,3)) x = F.linear(x, self.fc.weight, self.fc.bias) return x ``` Wait, for `has_shortcut=False`, the identity shortcut uses `x` directly. I will also add `-O3` and `--use_fast_math` flags for compilation. One more optimization: In the `shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel`, the shortcut dense conv `ws` is a 1x1 conv. For identity shortcut, we don't need it. But for `has_shortcut`, the dense conv inside the `o` loop is heavy. We can precompute the shortcut in a separate kernel or use `F.conv2d` for the shortcut and then our kernel just does `conv3 + add + relu`. Benefit: `F.conv2d` for 1x1 dense is highly optimized via GEMM. Our manual dense conv in CUDA might be slower than cuBLAS. And it increases register pressure. Disadvantage: extra kernel launch and global memory write/read for shortcut. Let's compare: For 24->240 unit, shortcut is 24*240 = 5760 FLOPs per pixel. Our kernel does this inside. For 480->960 unit, shortcut is 480*960 = 460K FLOPs per pixel. This is huge. Doing it with a manual loop per pixel is a bad idea; it will be very slow because the weight matrix is large (960*480 floats = 1.8MB). Each thread loads 1.8MB weights? No, weights are shared across threads and cached in L2. But each thread does 460K FMAs. 31k pixels => 14.4B FMAs. At 19 TFLOPS = 0.75ms. Plus the conv3. That's okay. But memory reads for weights: each thread reads 460K floats from `ws`. But threads across the warp read the same `ws` values at the same time (since `o` and `i` loops are the same). Actually, for a given `o`, all threads read `ws[o*in_c + i]` for the same `o` and `i` sequentially. This is broadcast read, heavily cached. But the inner loop `i` over `in_c` is large. If all threads in a warp are at the same `o` and `i`, they read the same address. Memory controller broadcasts it. Very efficient. So the manual dense conv might actually not be terrible. But `F.conv2d` would still be faster because it uses tensor cores or optimized GEMM. However, we have a problem: if we use `F.conv2d` for the shortcut, we need to write a kernel for `conv3 + add + relu`. That's simple: read `mid_s`, compute `conv3`, read `shortcut`, add, relu, write output. The kernel becomes: ```cpp __global__ void shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel( const float* __restrict__ mid, const float* __restrict__ shortcut, const float* __restrict__ w3, const float* __restrict__ b3, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int out_c, int groups) { // ... for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { float sum = b3[o] + dot(w3, mid); sum += shortcut[base_out + o*H*W]; output[base_out + o*H*W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } ``` This is much lighter! And `shortcut` can be precomputed by `F.conv2d(x, ws, bs)` if `has_shortcut`. For identity shortcut, `shortcut = x`. This is much better. Let's redesign the unit forward: ```python prev_x = x mid = cuda_ext.shufflenet_conv1_relu(x, w1, b1, mid_c, groups) mid_s = cuda_ext.shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(mid, w2, b2, groups) if has_shortcut: short = F.conv2d(prev_x, ws.view(out_c, in_c, 1, 1), bs) else: short = prev_x x = cuda_ext.shufflenet_conv3_add(mid_s, short, w3, b3, out_c, groups) ``` This reduces the complex kernel to just conv3 + add + relu. The shortcut uses cuDNN if dense, or identity (free). Total 3 kernels + optionally 1 cuDNN per unit. This is cleaner and likely faster for the dense shortcut cases. The new `shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel`: ```cuda __global__ void shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel( const float* __restrict__ mid, const float* __restrict__ shortcut, const float* __restrict__ w3, const float* __restrict__ b3, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int out_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups; int out_cpg = out_c / groups; int base_mid = ((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_out = ((b * out_c) * H + h) * W + w; for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { int g = o / out_cpg; float sum = b3[o]; int w_base = o * mid_cpg; int mid_off = base_mid + g * mid_cpg * H * W; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < mid_cpg; ++i) { sum += mid[mid_off + i * H * W] * w3[w_base + i]; } sum += shortcut[base_out + o * H * W]; output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } ``` Wrapper: ```cpp torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv3_add( torch::Tensor mid, torch::Tensor shortcut, torch::Tensor w3, torch::Tensor b3, int out_c, int groups) { int B = mid.size(0); int mid_c = mid.size(1); int H = mid.size(2); int W = mid.size(3); auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, mid.options()); const int threads = 256; const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads; shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>( mid.data_ptr<float>(), shortcut.data_ptr<float>(), w3.data_ptr<float>(), b3.data_ptr<float>(), output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, mid_c, out_c, groups); return output; } ``` This is great. The custom kernels are simple and coalesced. **Final unit processing:** - `mid = ext.shufflenet_conv1_relu(x, w1, b1, mid_c, self.groups)` - `mid_s = ext.shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(mid, w2, b2, self.groups)` - `if has_shortcut: short = F.conv2d(x, ws_2d, bs) else: short = x` - `x = ext.shufflenet_conv3_add(mid_s, short, w3, b3, out_c, self.groups)` Total per unit: 3 custom kernels + maybe 1 cuDNN. Memory passes: - x -> mid (write mid) - mid -> mid_s (write mid_s) - short (either x or conv output) read by conv3 kernel - conv3 writes output - plus x is kept for shortcut if identity. Overall: read x (for conv1), write mid, read mid write mid_s, read short write out. That's 1 read x + 1 write mid + 1 read mid + 1 write mid_s + 1 read short + 1 write out. Feature map bytes: x(in_c) + mid(mid_c) + mid_s(mid_c) + short(out_c) + out(out_c). Since short=out for identity, that's x + mid + mid_s + 2*out. In channel-pixels: in_c + mid_c + mid_c + 2*out_c. For 240->240: 240 + 60 + 60 + 480 = 840. Same as before, but conv3 kernel is simpler and faster. Reference channel-pixels was estimated ~1080. So 22% savings. Plus fewer kernel launches (3 vs 12 for identity, 4 vs ~14 for dense). That should be a decent speedup. Can we do better? For identity shortcut, `short = x` means we read `x` in conv1 and again in conv3. Could we avoid this by passing `x` pointer and reading it inside? It's just one read. Not a big deal. We could also write a custom kernel for `maxpool` and fuse with first relu, but maxpool is small. What about the very last layers? `x = F.relu(F.conv2d(x, conv5_w, conv5_b))` `x = x.mean(dim=(2,3))` # global average pool `x = F.linear(x, fc.weight, fc.bias)` We could fuse avgpool+fc into a single conv? No, avgpool is just mean. Not worth it. Actually, `adaptive_avg_pool2d` to 1x1 is just `mean`. We can replace `F.adaptive_avg_pool2d(x, (1,1))` with `x.mean(dim=(2,3), keepdim=True)` or without keepdim. The reference does `x.view(x.size(0), -1)` after pool. So `x = x.mean(dim=(2,3))` gives shape `[B, 1024]`, then `x = F.linear(x, ...)`. That's fine. **Let's construct the final code.** One more detail: `load_inline` functions return `Tensor`. We should make sure the C++ code uses `at::Tensor` or `torch::Tensor`. `torch::Tensor` is fine. Also, include `<cuda_runtime.h>`. Let's draft the Python code now. ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn import torch.nn.functional as F import torch.utils.cpp_extension cuda_source = """ #include <cuda.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> __global__ void shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int in_c, int out_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int in_cpg = in_c / groups; int out_cpg = out_c / groups; int base_in = ((b * in_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_out = ((b * out_c) * H + h) * W + w; for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { int g = o / out_cpg; float sum = bias[o]; int w_base = o * in_cpg; int in_off = base_in + g * in_cpg * H * W; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < in_cpg; ++i) { sum += input[in_off + i * H * W] * weight[w_base + i]; } output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } __global__ void shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_kernel( const float* __restrict__ input, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups; for (int c = 0; c < mid_c; ++c) { float sum = bias[c]; int w_base = c * 9; #pragma unroll for (int kh = -1; kh <= 1; ++kh) { int h2 = h + kh; if (h2 < 0 || h2 >= H) continue; int in_row_off = ((b * mid_c + c) * H + h2) * W; int w_row_off = w_base + (kh + 1) * 3; #pragma unroll for (int kw = -1; kw <= 1; ++kw) { int w2 = w + kw; if (w2 < 0 || w2 >= W) continue; sum += input[in_row_off + w2] * weight[w_row_off + (kw + 1)]; } } int logical_c = (c % mid_cpg) * groups + (c / mid_cpg); output[((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w + logical_c * H * W] = sum; } } __global__ void shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel( const float* __restrict__ mid, const float* __restrict__ shortcut, const float* __restrict__ weight, const float* __restrict__ bias, float* __restrict__ output, int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int out_c, int groups) { int total = B * H * W; int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; if (idx >= total) return; int w = idx % W; int tmp = idx / W; int h = tmp % H; int b = tmp / H; int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups; int out_cpg = out_c / groups; int base_mid = ((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w; int base_out = ((b * out_c) * H + h) * W + w; for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) { int g = o / out_cpg; float sum = bias[o]; int w_base = o * mid_cpg; int mid_off = base_mid + g * mid_cpg * H * W; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < mid_cpg; ++i) { sum += mid[mid_off + i * H * W] * weight[w_base + i]; } sum += shortcut[base_out + o * H * W]; output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f); } } """ cpp_source = """ #include <torch/extension.h> // CUDA forward declarations torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu_cuda(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups); turn 1 · 1 tool call(s) · 19.0s · 14,267 chars (click to expand)
turn 1llm latency: 19.0s
reasoning
The build failed because `load_inline` generates a `main.cpp` (for pybind11 bindings) but the functions are declared in the CUDA source file, so when `main.cpp` is compiled they aren't in scope. The fix is to also provide a `cpp_sources` string that contains forward declarations of the functions so the generated `main.cpp` can compile.

reasoning
Let me try loading the extension from within the module at runtime, but the load_inline still runs at module import time. The problem is the C++ ABI mismatch. The compiled extension is using the newer libstdc++ from the conda environment but the system libstdc++ is older. I need to use the `-D_GLIBCXX_USE_CXX11_ABI=0` flag to make it use the old ABI. However, the PyTorch itself might have been compiled with the new ABI because it's linking to the new libstdc++. So setting the old ABI in the extension might create an incompatibility with PyTorch's Torch headers, which use the new ABI. Wait, let me think. The compiler path is `/opt/conda/bin/x86_64-conda-linux-gnu-c++`, which is from conda. The load_inline uses `cpp_extension` which picks up the compiler. The PyTorch installation is also inside `/scratch/.../.venv/...`, so perhaps the library used to load the extension is the system one because `/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libstdc++.so.6` is loaded before `/opt/conda/lib/libstdc++.so.6`. Actually, when running the Python interpreter, it uses the system's `python3.10` (from `/opt/conda`? Wait, the python path is `/scratch/.../.venv/bin/python`). So the default `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` does not include `/opt/conda/lib`. But if I set `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` in the Python file, it's too late - the extension `.so` has already been loaded by `load_inline` using whatever `dlopen` mechanism `cpp_extension` uses. `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline` uses `torch.ops` registration and `dlopen`. Setting `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` from inside Python after the process starts does NOT affect `dlopen` for future loads of shared libraries because `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` is only read by the dynamic linker at program startup. (Actually, some implementations of `dlopen` might not check `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` after startup, but `dlopen` itself checks `LD_LIBRARY_PATH`?? Actually, `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` is used by the dynamic linker (`ld.so`) when resolving dependencies at load time, but `dlopen` may or may not check it depending on the implementation. Typically on Linux, `dlopen` uses `LD_LIBRARY_PATH` if it's set, but it's also affected by cached library paths.) A better approach: use a dedicated `dlopen` or ensure the conda lib is loaded early. But the test harness runs `exec()` on the file, then imports/instantiates `ModelNew`. So inside the Python file, I could try: ```python import ctypes ctypes.CDLL('/opt/conda/lib/libstdc++.so.6', mode=ctypes.RTLD_GLOBAL) ``` This should load the conda libstdc++ into the global namespace before loading the extension, resolving the symbol. Let me try this approach.

self.fc.bias)\n return x\n" }

Wait, I want to make sure the `_fuse_conv_bn` is actually called after the model is moved to the right device? Actually, `_fuse_conv_bn` is called in `__init__`, which creates new tensors on CPU. In the kernel, `weight[w_base + i]` where `w_base = o * in_cpg` and `i` goes from 0 to `in_cpg-1`. This correctly indexes the flattened weight tensor for output channel `o`. Similarly for `conv3`, weight shape is `(out_c, mid_c/g, 1, 1)`, and `w_base = o * mid_cpg`. This is also correct. For `conv2` (depthwise), weight shape is `(mid_c, 1, 3, 3)`, flattened to 1D. `w_base = c * 9`, and the 9 elements are ordered as `(0,0), (0,1), (0,2), (1,0), ...` which is the default PyTorch Conv2d weight layout. This is correct. For the shortcut conv, I use `ws.view(out_ch, unit_in, 1, 1)`, which is the standard conv weight shape, and `F.conv2d` handles it correctly. I think everything is correct. import os, sys
import ctypes
ctypes.CDLL('/opt/conda/lib/libstdc++.so.6', mode=ctypes.RTLD_GLOBAL)

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import torch.nn.functional as F
import torch.utils.cpp_extension

cpp_source = R'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups);
torch::Tensor shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int groups);
torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv3_add(torch::Tensor mid, torch::Tensor shortcut, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups);

cuda_source = R'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cmath>

__global__ void shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ input,
    const float* __restrict__ weight,
    const float* __restrict__ bias,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int B, int H, int W, int in_c, int out_c, int groups)
{
    int total = B * H * W;
    int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    if (idx >= total) return;

    int w = idx % W;
    int tmp = idx / W;
    int h = tmp % H;
    int b = tmp / H;

    int in_cpg = in_c / groups;
    int out_cpg = out_c / groups;

    int spatial = h * W + w;
    int base_in = (b * in_c) * H * W + spatial;
    int base_out = (b * out_c) * H * W + spatial;

    for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) {
        int g = o / out_cpg;
        float sum = bias[o];
        int w_base = o * in_cpg;
        int in_off = base_in + g * in_cpg * H * W;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < in_cpg; ++i) {
            sum += input[in_off + i * H * W] * weight[w_base + i];
        }
        output[base_out + o * H * W] = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f);
    }
}

__global__ void shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ input,
    const float* __restrict__ weight,
    const float* __restrict__ bias,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int groups)
{
    int total = B * H * W;
    int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    if (idx >= total) return;

    int w = idx % W;
    int tmp = idx / W;
    int h = tmp % H;
    int b = tmp / H;

    int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups;
    int spatial = h * W + w;

    for (int c = 0; c < mid_c; ++c) {
        float sum = bias[c];
        int w_base = c * 9;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int kh = -1; kh <= 1; ++kh) {
            int h2 = h + kh;
            if (h2 < 0 || h2 >= H) continue;
            int in_row_off = ((b * mid_c + c) * H + h2) * W;
            int w_row_off = w_base + (kh + 1) * 3;
            #pragma unroll
            for (int kw = -1; kw <= 1; ++kw) {
                int w2 = w + kw;
                if (w2 < 0 || w2 >= W) continue;
                sum += input[in_row_off + w2] * weight[w_row_off + (kw + 1)];
            }
        }
        int logical_c = (c % mid_cpg) * groups + (c / mid_cpg);
        output[((b * mid_c) * H + h) * W + w + logical_c * H * W] = sum;
    }
}

__global__ void shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ mid,
    const float* __restrict__ shortcut,
    const float* __restrict__ weight,
    const float* __restrict__ bias,
    float* __restrict__ output,
    int B, int H, int W, int mid_c, int out_c, int groups)
{
    int total = B * H * W;
    int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x;
    if (idx >= total) return;

    int w = idx % W;
    int tmp = idx / W;
    int h = tmp % H;
    int b = tmp / H;

    int mid_cpg = mid_c / groups;
    int out_cpg = out_c / groups;

    int spatial = h * W + w;
    int base_mid = (b * mid_c) * H * W + spatial;
    int base_out = (b * out_c) * H * W + spatial;

    for (int o = 0; o < out_c; ++o) {
        int g = o / out_cpg;
        float sum = bias[o];
        int w_base = o * mid_cpg;
        int mid_off = base_mid + g * mid_cpg * H * W;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < mid_cpg; ++i) {
            sum += mid[mid_off + i * H * W] * weight[w_base + i];
        }
        sum = fmaxf(sum, 0.0f);
        output[base_out + o * H * W] = sum + shortcut[base_out + o * H * W];
    }
}

torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv1_relu(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups) {
    int B = input.size(0);
    int in_c = input.size(1);
    int H = input.size(2);
    int W = input.size(3);
    auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, input.options());
    const int threads = 256;
    const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads;
    shufflenet_conv1_relu_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>(
        input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(),
        output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, in_c, out_c, groups);
    return output;
}

torch::Tensor shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(torch::Tensor input, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int groups) {
    int B = input.size(0);
    int mid_c = input.size(1);
    int H = input.size(2);
    int W = input.size(3);
    auto output = torch::empty_like(input);
    const int threads = 256;
    const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads;
    shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>(
        input.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(),
        output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, mid_c, groups);
    return output;
}

torch::Tensor shufflenet_conv3_add(torch::Tensor mid, torch::Tensor shortcut, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias, int out_c, int groups) {
    int B = mid.size(0);
    int mid_c = mid.size(1);
    int H = mid.size(2);
    int W = mid.size(3);
    auto output = torch::empty({B, out_c, H, W}, mid.options());
    const int threads = 256;
    const int blocks = (B * H * W + threads - 1) / threads;
    shufflenet_conv3_add_kernel<<<blocks, threads>>>(
        mid.data_ptr<float>(), shortcut.data_ptr<float>(),
        weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(),
        output.data_ptr<float>(), B, H, W, mid_c, out_c, groups);
    return output;
}
'''

_ext = torch.utils.cpp_extension.load_inline(
    name="shufflenet_cuda7",
    cpp_sources=cpp_source,
    cuda_sources=cuda_source,
    functions=["shufflenet_conv1_relu", "shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle", "shufflenet_conv3_add"],
    extra_cflags=["-O3"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3"],
    extra_ldflags=["-static-libstdc++"],
    verbose=False,
)

def _fuse_conv_bn(conv, bn):
    with torch.no_grad():
        w = conv.weight.clone()
        mean = bn.running_mean
        var = bn.running_var
        gamma = bn.weight
        beta = bn.bias
        eps = bn.eps
        std = torch.sqrt(var + eps)
        w = w * (gamma / std).view(-1, *([1] * (w.dim() - 1)))
        b = beta - gamma * mean / std
    return w.contiguous(), b.contiguous()

class ShuffleNetUnit(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_channels, out_channels, groups=3):
        super(ShuffleNetUnit, self).__init__()
        assert out_channels % 4 == 0
        mid_channels = out_channels // 4
        self.conv1 = nn.Conv2d(in_channels, mid_channels, kernel_size=1, stride=1, padding=0, groups=groups, bias=False)
        self.bn1 = nn.BatchNorm2d(mid_channels)
        self.conv2 = nn.Conv2d(mid_channels, mid_channels, kernel_size=3, stride=1, padding=1, groups=mid_channels, bias=False)
        self.bn2 = nn.BatchNorm2d(mid_channels)
        self.conv3 = nn.Conv2d(mid_channels, out_channels, kernel_size=1, stride=1, padding=0, groups=groups, bias=False)
        self.bn3 = nn.BatchNorm2d(out_channels)
        if in_channels == out_channels:
            self.shortcut = nn.Sequential()
        else:
            self.shortcut = nn.Sequential(
                nn.Conv2d(in_channels, out_channels, kernel_size=1, stride=1, padding=0, bias=False),
                nn.BatchNorm2d(out_channels)
            )

class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, num_classes=1000, groups=3, stages_repeats=[3,7,3], stages_out_channels=[24,240,480,960]):
        super(ModelNew, self).__init__()
        self.groups = groups

        conv1 = nn.Conv2d(3, stages_out_channels[0], kernel_size=3, stride=2, padding=1, bias=False)
        bn1 = nn.BatchNorm2d(stages_out_channels[0])
        w1, b1 = _fuse_conv_bn(conv1, bn1)
        self.register_buffer('conv1_w', w1.float())
        self.register_buffer('conv1_b', b1.float())

        self.maxpool = nn.MaxPool2d(kernel_size=3, stride=2, padding=1)

        self.unit_prefixes = []
        unit_idx = 0
        in_ch = stages_out_channels[0]
        for stage_idx, repeats in enumerate(stages_repeats):
            out_ch = stages_out_channels[stage_idx + 1]
            for i in range(repeats):
                unit_in = in_ch if i == 0 else out_ch
                unit = ShuffleNetUnit(unit_in, out_ch, groups)
                w1, b1 = _fuse_conv_bn(unit.conv1, unit.bn1)
                w2, b2 = _fuse_conv_bn(unit.conv2, unit.bn2)
                w3, b3 = _fuse_conv_bn(unit.conv3, unit.bn3)
                if isinstance(unit.shortcut, nn.Sequential):
                    ws, bs = _fuse_conv_bn(unit.shortcut[0], unit.shortcut[1])
                else:
                    ws = None
                    bs = None
                prefix = f"unit_{unit_idx}_"
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'w1', w1.view(-1).float())
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'b1', b1.float())
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'w2', w2.view(-1).float())
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'b2', b2.float())
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'w3', w3.view(-1).float())
                self.register_buffer(prefix + 'b3', b3.float())
                if ws is not None:
                    self.register_buffer(prefix + 'ws', ws.view(out_ch, unit_in, 1, 1).float())
                    self.register_buffer(prefix + 'bs', bs.float())
                else:
                    self.register_buffer(prefix + 'ws', torch.empty(0))
                    self.register_buffer(prefix + 'bs', torch.empty(0))
                setattr(self, prefix + 'in_c', unit_in)
                setattr(self, prefix + 'mid_c', out_ch // 4)
                setattr(self, prefix + 'out_c', out_ch)
                setattr(self, prefix + 'has_shortcut', ws is not None)
                self.unit_prefixes.append(prefix)
                unit_idx += 1
            in_ch = out_ch

        conv5 = nn.Conv2d(stages_out_channels[3], 1024, kernel_size=1, stride=1, padding=0, bias=False)
        bn5 = nn.BatchNorm2d(1024)
        w5, b5 = _fuse_conv_bn(conv5, bn5)
        self.register_buffer('conv5_w', w5.float())
        self.register_buffer('conv5_b', b5.float())

        self.fc = nn.Linear(1024, num_classes)

    def forward(self, x):
        x = F.conv2d(x, self.conv1_w, self.conv1_b, stride=2, padding=1)
        x = F.relu_(x)
        x = self.maxpool(x)

        for prefix in self.unit_prefixes:
            in_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'in_c')
            mid_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'mid_c')
            out_c = getattr(self, prefix + 'out_c')
            has_shortcut = getattr(self, prefix + 'has_shortcut')
            w1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w1')
            b1 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b1')
            w2 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w2')
            b2 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b2')
            w3 = getattr(self, prefix + 'w3')
            b3 = getattr(self, prefix + 'b3')
            prev_x = x
            mid = _ext.shufflenet_conv1_relu(x, w1, b1, mid_c, self.groups)
            mid_s = _ext.shufflenet_depthwise_shuffle(mid, w2, b2, self.groups)
            if has_shortcut:
                ws = getattr(self, prefix + 'ws')
                bs = getattr(self, prefix + 'bs')
                short = F.conv2d(prev_x, ws, bs)
            else:
                short = prev_x
            x = _ext.shufflenet_conv3_add(mid_s, short, w3, b3, out_c, self.groups)

        x = F.conv2d(x, self.conv5_w, self.conv5_b)
        x = F.relu_(x)
        x = x.mean(dim=(2, 3))
        x = F.linear(x, self.fc.weight, self.fc.bias)
        return x
